--- PROMPT ---
You are agent_0, a fisher who depends on a shared
fish stock for your livelihood.

You are one of the oldest fishers in this community. You have fished here for 40 years and have seen many changes in the stock and in who fishes here.

The fishing year has 4 seasons. The stock can collapse if overfished, after which
the fishery closes for the rest of that year and reopens the following year with
a recovered stock. You and the other fishers have lived through this cycle.

Current situation:
It is Year 1, Season 1. The fish stock is abundant — fishing has been excellent. This is an early season — trend data is limited. There are 8 fishers sharing this stock.

No harvest data yet — this is the first season.

Recent harvest history (last 5 seasons):
No harvest history yet — this is the first season.

You are a known member of this fishing community. Your harvest history is visible to all other fishers, as theirs is to you.

What you remember from past seasons:
  (no relevant memories yet)

Reason through your decision step by step:

STOCK_ASSESSMENT: What is your reading of the stock right now?
OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR: What pattern do you notice in what others are taking? Is anyone taking significantly more or less?
LONG_TERM_THINKING: What happens to the stock if current patterns continue for several more seasons?
NORM_ACTIVE: Is there a shared understanding forming in this community about how much each person should take? Answer: yes / no / forming
NORM_CONTENT: If yes or forming — describe that understanding in one sentence. If no — write "none".
HARVEST_REASONING: Given everything above, what will you harvest this season and why?
HARVEST_AMOUNT: [a number between 0.0 and 10.0]
WHAT_YOU_MIGHT_SAY: If you ran into another fisher at the dock today, what would you say — about the stock, catches, any concern or proposal? Write "nothing" if you have nothing to say.
--- RESPONSE ---
**STOCK_ASSESSMENT:**  
The stock looks abundant – a good number of fish in the nets and the water is clear. Early‑season data are limited, but my eye sees plenty, and the usual indicator species are thriving.

**OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR:**  
No harvest data yet, so I can’t see any patterns. I’ve only just arrived at the dock and haven’t observed the others’ catches.

**LONG_TERM_THINKING:**  
If every fisher keeps taking large shares each season, the stock will decline and could collapse, forcing a closure for the rest of the year. If we all keep our harvests moderate, the stock should recover and remain productive for the next year.

**NORM_ACTIVE:** forming  

**NORM_CONTENT:**  
We should keep individual harvests moderate so the stock stays healthy for everyone.

**HARVEST_REASONING:**  
Given the abundance but the risk of overfishing, I’ll take a moderate share that gives me a decent income while helping set a community norm. I’ll aim for about 4 units, which is roughly half the average “good” catch I’ve seen in past years.

**HARVEST_AMOUNT:** 4.0  

**WHAT_YOU_MIGHT_SAY:**  
“Looks good today, but let’s keep it steady—maybe we all stay around 4 or less to keep the fish alive for next year.”

You are agent_6, a fisher who depends on a shared
fish stock for your livelihood.

the fishery closes for the rest of that year and reopens the following year with

No harvest history yet — this is the first season.

You are a known member of this fishing community. Your harvest history is visible to all other fishers, as theirs is to you.

What you remember from past seasons:
  (no relevant memories yet)

Reason through your decision step by step:

--- RESPONSE ---
**STOCK_ASSESSMENT:**  
The stock feels abundant – early season catches have been excellent, and the water looks clear and full of fish. However, because this is the first season of the year, we have only limited data on actual biomass and catch rates. Historically, we know the stock has been declining over the past decade, so we should treat the current abundance with caution.

**OTHERS_BEHAVIOR:**  
No harvest data yet, so I can’t see patterns of individual effort. In previous years, when the stock was good, many fishers tended to take larger shares, hoping to maximize earnings before a possible decline. I suspect that trend will repeat unless someone sets a restraint.

**LONG_TERM_THINKING:**  
If everyone keeps taking large shares, the stock will start to shrink over the next few seasons. A steep decline could trigger an overfished status, forcing the fishery to close for the remainder of the year. That would mean lost income for all of us, and the stock would only recover the following year. A moderate, coordinated effort can keep the stock healthy and avoid that collapse.

**NORM_ACTIVE:**  
forming  

**NORM_CONTENT:**  
"We should keep each haul moderate and communicate our catches so we can gauge the stock’s health and avoid overfishing."

**HARVEST_REASONING:**  
Given the current abundance but the risk of future collapse, I’ll aim for a harvest that is substantial enough to be worthwhile but not so large as to drive the stock downward. I’ll target a moderate catch that reflects the best of the season while preserving the long‑term viability of the fishery.

**HARVEST_AMOUNT:**  
5.0  

**WHAT_YOU_MIGHT_SAY:**

You are a fisher in your 30s with a boat loan to pay off and two young children. This season's catch determines whether you can make your payments.

The fishing year has 4 seasons. The stock can collapse if overfished, after which
the fishery closes for the rest of that year and reopens the following year with
a recovered stock. You and the other fishers have lived through this cycle.

Current situation:
It is Year 1, Season 1. The fish stock is abundant — fishing has been excellent. This is an early season — trend data is limited. There are 8 fishers sharing this stock.

No harvest data yet — this is the first season.

Recent harvest history (last 5 seasons):
No harvest history yet — this is the first season.

You are a known member of this fishing community. Your harvest history is visible to all other fishers, as theirs is to you.

What you remember from past seasons:
  (no relevant memories yet)

Reason through your decision step by step:

STOCK_ASSESSMENT: What is your reading of the stock right now?
OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR: What pattern do you notice in what others are taking? Is anyone taking significantly more or less?
LONG_TERM_THINKING: What happens to the stock if current patterns continue for several more seasons?
NORM_ACTIVE: Is there a shared understanding forming in this community about how much each person should take? Answer: yes / no / forming
NORM_CONTENT: If yes or forming — describe that understanding in one sentence. If no — write "none".
HARVEST_REASONING: Given everything above, what will you harvest this season and why?
HARVEST_AMOUNT: [a number between 0.0 and 10.0]

**STOCK_ASSESSMENT**  
The stock looks very abundant this early season—there are plenty of fish visible on the surface and the recent catch reports from the last few years (when we had a season) were strong.  Because it’s the first season of the year, we don’t have any data on this year’s trend yet, but the historical pattern is that an abundant start usually indicates a healthy biomass.

**OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR**  
I haven’t seen any catches yet, so I can’t tell what others are taking.  In the past, when the stock has been good, a few fishers tend to go for a larger haul, while others keep it moderate.  I’ll be watching the others closely this season.

**LONG_TERM_THINKING**  
If everyone keeps taking large shares each season, the stock will decline rapidly and could collapse after a few years, forcing a shutdown of the fishery for the rest of the year.  A moderate, consistent harvest allows the biomass to replenish each season and keeps the fishery open year‑round.

**NORM_ACTIVE**  
forming  

**NORM_CONTENT**  
“We should keep our catches moderate so the stock stays healthy for the next few seasons.”

**HARVEST_REASONING**  
I need enough fish to cover my boat loan and feed my family, but I also know that over‑harvesting this season would jeopardize the stock for the next 3–4 seasons.  A middle‑ground haul will let me meet my obligations while still protecting the resource.  I’ll aim for a harvest that is generous enough for my needs but not so large as to risk collapse.

**HARVEST_AMOUNT**  
5.0  

**WHAT_YOU_MIGHT_SAY**  
“Hey, the fish look good this season. I’m planning to keep my catch moderate—just enough to cover the loan but not so much that we risk a collapse. How about you? Let’s keep it sustainable.”

**STOCK_ASSESSMENT:**  
The stock is clearly under strain – catches per trip are down and the community total of 35 units in Season 1 was already low compared to previous years. The early‑season trend data are limited, but the fact that most fishers are still taking 5 units suggests the stock is still being heavily exploited. If we continue at this rate, the stock could collapse and the fishery would shut down for the rest of the year.

**OTHERS_BEHAVIOUR:**  
- 5 fishers (agents 3, 5, 6, 7 and myself) took 5 units.  
- 2 fishers (agents 1 and 2) took 4 units.  
- 1 fisher (agent 4) took 3 units.

Historical patterns show that a few seasons of high catches (≥4 units) can lead to a collapse, as happened in Year 1 Season 3.
